SECTION 6 — FAQ
1. Cost — How much does a 200Tdi or 300Tdi engine replacement cost?
A reconditioned 200Tdi or 300Tdi typically costs £3,000–£5,500 supply only, with used units from £1,000–£2,000. Fitting adds £900–£2,500 depending on labour rates and vehicle access.
2. Reliability — Is the 200Tdi / 300Tdi a reliable engine?
Yes — both are widely considered among the most reliable Land Rover engines ever built. Their fully mechanical fuel systems, lack of complex electronics, and simple OHV design make them exceptionally durable, with many exceeding 250,000–300,000 miles.
3. Common failure — What is the most common 200Tdi / 300Tdi failure?
Head gasket failure from overheating is the most common serious issue — typically caused by cooling system neglect. Early 300Tdi units also suffered timing belt idler alignment problems, and 200Tdi crank dampers can disintegrate.
4. Fitment — Which Land Rover models use the 200Tdi / 300Tdi?
The 200Tdi and 300Tdi powered three core Land Rover models: the Defender (90/110), Discovery Series 1, and Range Rover Classic.
5. Longevity — How long does the 200Tdi / 300Tdi last?
With proper maintenance, 200Tdi and 300Tdi engines routinely exceed 250,000 miles, with many well-maintained examples reaching 300,000+ miles. Regular timing belt changes every 80,000 km (~50,000 miles) and cooling system maintenance are key to achieving this lifespan.

SECTION 6 — FAQ
1. Cost — How much does a TD5 engine replacement cost?
A reconditioned TD5 long engine typically costs £3,600–£5,500 supply only, with a full fitted replacement around £5,980 including VAT. Used units can be found from £400–£1,500 depending on condition and provenance.
2. Reliability — Is the TD5 a reliable engine?
Yes — the TD5 is widely regarded as one of Land Rover's most dependable modern diesels, with many exceeding 200,000 miles. Its cast-iron block and five-cylinder design are robust, though the electronic injection system requires proper maintenance.
3. Common failure — What is the most common TD5 failure?
The most serious TD5 failure is the oil pump bolt working loose — a known issue on early engines that can cause sudden loss of oil pressure and catastrophic bearing failure. Other common issues include injector wiring loom oil contamination (oil wicking up from the injectors) and diesel dilution from leaking injector seals.
4. Fitment — Which Land Rover models use the TD5?
The TD5 powered three Land Rover models: the Defender (90/110/130) from 1998–2006, the Discovery Series 2 from 1998–2004, and the Range Rover P38A from 1998–2002.
5. Longevity — How long does the TD5 last?
With proper maintenance — regular oil changes, injector loom checks, and addressing the oil pump bolt on early engines — TD5 engines routinely exceed 200,000 miles, with many well-maintained examples reaching 250,000–350,000+ km (~155,000–217,000+ miles).

SECTION 6 — FAQ
1. Cost — How much does an Ingenium 2.0 diesel engine replacement cost?
A reconditioned Ingenium 2.0 diesel typically costs £3,500–£5,800 supply only, varying by power output and specific sub‑variant. Fitting adds £900–£1,700 depending on labour rates and vehicle model.
2. Reliability — Is the Ingenium 2.0 diesel a reliable engine?
It is a capable and efficient modern diesel (3.5★), but its reputation is mixed due to pre‑2019 timing chain tensioner failures and oil‑dilution from DPF regens. Post‑2019 revisions are significantly improved.
3. Common failure — What is the most common Ingenium 2.0 diesel failure?
Pre‑2019 timing chain tensioner failure is the most critical — it can cause sudden chain stretch and catastrophic valve/piston interference. Other common issues include EGR cooler leaks and oil dilution from incomplete DPF regenerations on short‑trip vehicles.
4. Fitment — Which Land Rover models use the Ingenium 2.0 diesel?
It powers the Discovery Sport (L550), Evoque (L551), Velar (L560), and Defender (L663) — spanning 150–240 hp outputs.
5. Shared — Is the Land Rover Ingenium 2.0 diesel the same as Jaguar's version?
Yes — the 204DTD and 224DT engine codes are shared across both brands. The engine is mechanically identical between Land Rover and Jaguar fitments, though ECU calibrations and ancillaries differ by model.

SECTION 6 — FAQ
1. Cost — How much does an Ingenium 2.0 petrol engine replacement cost?
A reconditioned Ingenium 2.0 petrol typically costs £3,000–£5,000 supply only, varying by power output and specific sub‑variant. Fitting adds £900–£1,700 depending on labour rates and vehicle model.
2. Reliability — Is the Ingenium 2.0 petrol a reliable engine?
Yes — the 204PT is more reliable than its diesel counterpart (4.0★). Its direct-injection turbo design is well-proven, though cooling system components require regular maintenance and the water pump is a known wear item.
3. Common failure — What is the most common Ingenium 2.0 petrol failure?
Water pump failure and coolant leaks from plastic fittings are the most common issues — typically occurring from 60,000–80,000 miles. Other reported problems include occasional timing chain stretch and PCV valve failure.
4. Fitment — Which Land Rover models use the Ingenium 2.0 petrol?
It powers the Discovery Sport (L550), Evoque (L551), Velar (L560), and Defender (L663) — spanning 200–300 hp outputs across P200, P250, and P300 variants.
5. Shared — Is the Land Rover Ingenium 2.0 petrol the same as Jaguar's version?
Yes — the 204PT engine code is shared across both brands. The engine is mechanically identical between Land Rover and Jaguar fitments, though ECU calibrations and ancillaries differ by model.

SECTION 6 — FAQ
1. Cost — How much does a 276DT (2.7 TDV6) engine replacement cost?
A reconditioned 276DT TDV6 typically costs £5,000–£7,500 supply only, varying by spec and rebuild quality. A used unit can be found from £2,800–£4,500, but history is critical. Fitting adds £900–£2,000 depending on labour rates.
2. Reliability — Is the 276DT (2.7 TDV6) a reliable engine?
It is a refined and capable V6 (3.5★) — but its reputation is compromised by the well‑documented oil pump housing failure. This single point of weakness can cause sudden oil pressure loss and catastrophic bottom‑end failure.
3. Common failure — What is the most common 276DT failure?
Oil pump housing failure is the most serious — a weak point at the tensioner mount causes the pump to fail suddenly, killing oil pressure and destroying bearings. Cold start knock is the early warning sign. Other issues include turbo failure and EGR clogging.
4. Fitment — Which Land Rover models use the 276DT?
The 276DT powered the Discovery 3 (L319) from 2004–2009 and the Range Rover Sport (L320) from 2005–2010.
5. Shared — Is the Land Rover 276DT the same as Jaguar's version?
Yes — the 276DT is shared with Jaguar fitments in the XF (X250) and XJ (X351). The engine is mechanically identical, though ECU calibrations and ancillaries differ by model.

SECTION 6 — FAQ
1. Cost — How much does a 306DT (3.0 TDV6/SDV6) engine replacement cost?
A reconditioned 306DT TDV6/SDV6 typically costs £6,500–£9,500 supply only, varying by power output and specification. A used unit can be found from £3,500–£5,500, but history is absolutely critical. Fitting adds £1,000–£2,000 depending on labour rates.
2. Reliability — Is the 306DT (3.0 TDV6/SDV6) a reliable engine?
The 306DT has a mixed reputation (3.0★). While many examples exceed 150,000 miles, the well‑documented crankshaft bearing failure can strike without warning, particularly on poorly maintained examples. Scrupulous oil change intervals are essential.
3. Common failure — What is the most common 306DT failure?
Crankshaft bearing failure is the most catastrophic — the tin‑aluminium bearing coating can fatigue, causing sudden failure and bottom‑end destruction. Cold‑start knock is the early warning sign. Other common issues include turbo contamination and oil pump problems.
4. Fitment — Which Land Rover models use the 306DT?
The 306DT powers the Discovery 4 (L319) and Discovery 5 (L462), Range Rover Sport (L494/L461), Range Rover (L405/L460), and Defender (L663) — spanning 211–306 hp outputs across TDV6, SDV6, D250, D300, and D350 variants.
5. Shared — Is the Land Rover 306DT the same as Jaguar's version?
Yes — the 306DT is shared with Jaguar fitments in the XF, XJ, and F‑Pace. The engine is mechanically identical, though ECU calibrations and ancillaries differ by model.

SECTION 6 — FAQ
1. Cost — How much does a 448DT (4.4 SDV8/TDV8) engine replacement cost?
A reconditioned 448DT SDV8 typically costs £6,000–£9,000 supply only, varying by specification and rebuild quality. Used units can be found from £3,500–£6,000, but provenance is essential. Fitting adds £1,200–£2,500 depending on labour rates.
2. Reliability — Is the 448DT (4.4 SDV8/TDV8) a reliable engine?
Yes — the 448DT is widely regarded as the most durable of Land Rover's modern V8 diesels (4.0★). Its robust bottom-end design lacks the catastrophic failure modes of the smaller V6 units. The main watchpoints are oil cooler leaks and coolant crossover pipe corrosion.
3. Common failure — What is the most common 448DT failure?
Oil cooler leaks in the V of the engine and coolant crossover pipe failure are the most common issues — typically occurring at 100,000+ miles. Alternator failure is also reported due to oil contamination from cooler leaks. No catastrophic bottom-end design flaws are known.
4. Fitment — Which Land Rover models use the 448DT?
The 448DT powers the Range Rover (L405) SDV8/TDV8 from 2012–2020, the Range Rover Sport (L494) SDV8 from 2013–2020, and the Discovery 4 (L319) SDV8 from 2014–2016.
5. Shared — Is the Land Rover 448DT the same as Jaguar's version?
Yes — the 448DT is shared with Jaguar fitments in the XJ (X351) and XF (X260). The engine is mechanically identical, though ECU calibrations and ancillaries differ by model.

SECTION 6 — FAQ
1. Cost — How much does an AJ133 (5.0 V8) engine replacement cost?
A reconditioned AJ133 V8 typically costs £5,500–£9,000 supply only, varying by specification (NA vs SC) and rebuild quality. Used units can be found from £3,000–£5,500, but provenance is critical. Fitting adds £900–£2,000 depending on labour rates.
2. Reliability — Is the AJ133 (5.0 V8) a reliable engine?
The AJ133 has a mixed reputation (3.5★). Pre‑2013 timing chain tensioner failure is a known issue, and coolant system leaks are common. Post‑2013 revisions improved durability significantly, making later examples far more dependable.
3. Common failure — What is the most common AJ133 failure?
Pre‑2013 timing chain tensioner wear is the most critical — it can cause chain stretch and catastrophic interference. Coolant leaks from crossover pipes and water pump failure are also frequent. Supercharger coupler wear (on SC versions) is another common issue.
4. Fitment — Which Land Rover models use the AJ133?
The AJ133 powers the Range Rover (L405) with both naturally aspirated and supercharged versions, and the Range Rover Sport (L494) with the supercharged 5.0 V8.
5. Shared — Is the Land Rover AJ133 the same as Jaguar's version?
Yes — the AJ133 is shared with Jaguar fitments in the XF, XJ, XK, and F‑Type. The engine is mechanically identical, though ECU calibrations and ancillaries differ by model.

SECTION 6 — FAQ
1. Cost — How much does an AJ20D6 (Ingenium 3.0 I6 Diesel) engine replacement cost?
A reconditioned AJ20D6 Ingenium diesel typically costs £4,500–£7,500 supply only, varying by power output and specification. Used units can be found from £2,500–£4,500, but provenance is critical. Fitting adds £1,000–£2,000 depending on labour rates.
2. Reliability — Is the AJ20D6 (Ingenium 3.0 I6 Diesel) a reliable engine?
The AJ20D6 is a modern and capable straight‑six diesel (4.0★) with strong real‑world feedback. Early examples (2020–2021) have reported AdBlue system and EGR cooler issues, but JLR has addressed these with software updates and hardware revisions.
3. Common failure — What is the most common AJ20D6 failure?
AdBlue system issues (NOx sensors, heaters, and crystallisation) are the most common reported problems, particularly on early 2020–2021 vehicles. EGR cooler leaks and occasional DPF clogging from urban use are also reported. No major bottom‑end issues are known.
4. Fitment — Which Land Rover models use the AJ20D6?
The AJ20D6 powers the latest‑generation Range Rover (L460), Range Rover Sport (L461), and Defender (L663) — spanning D250, D300, and D350 outputs.
5. Shared — Is the Land Rover AJ20D6 the same as Jaguar's version?
Yes — the AJ20D6 is shared with Jaguar fitments in the F‑Pace, XF, and XJ. The engine is mechanically identical, though ECU calibrations and ancillaries differ by model.

SECTION 6 — FAQ
1. Cost — How much does an AJ20P6 (Ingenium 3.0 I6 Petrol / P400) engine replacement cost?
A reconditioned AJ20P6 Ingenium petrol typically costs £4,500–£7,500 supply only, varying by specification and rebuild quality. Used units can be found from £2,500–£4,500, but provenance is critical. Fitting adds £1,000–£2,000 depending on labour rates.
2. Reliability — Is the AJ20P6 (Ingenium 3.0 I6 Petrol / P400) a reliable engine?
The AJ20P6 is a modern and capable straight‑six petrol (4.0★) with positive real‑world feedback. Early examples have reported cooling system issues, but JLR has addressed many of these with software updates and revisions. Regular maintenance is essential.
3. Common failure — What is the most common AJ20P6 failure?
Cooling system issues are the most common reported problems — including water pump leaks, coolant hose failures, and occasional thermostat housing cracks. Other reported issues include oil leaks from the timing cover and occasional software glitches in the MHEV system.
4. Fitment — Which Land Rover models use the AJ20P6?
The AJ20P6 (P400) powers the latest‑generation Range Rover (L460), Range Rover Sport (L461), and Defender (L663).
5. Shared — Is the Land Rover AJ20P6 the same as Jaguar's version?
Yes — the AJ20P6 is shared with Jaguar fitments in the F‑Pace, XF, and XJ. The engine is mechanically identical, though ECU calibrations and ancillaries differ by model.

SECTION 6 — FAQ
1. Cost — How much does an M57 Td6 engine replacement cost?
A reconditioned M57 Td6 typically costs £1,500–£2,500 supply only, with used units from £600–£1,200. Fitting adds £800–£1,200 depending on labour rates and vehicle access.
2. Reliability — Is the M57 Td6 a reliable engine?
Yes — the M57 is widely considered one of BMW's most reliable diesel engines, winning the International Engine of the Year award in its class for 1999–2002 and again in 2009. With proper maintenance, many exceed 200,000 miles.
3. Common failure — What is the most common M57 Td6 failure?
Swirl flap failure is the most critical — these metal flaps in the intake manifold can break off and be sucked into the engine, causing catastrophic cylinder damage. Turbocharger wear, injector issues, and timing chain stretch are also common.
4. Fitment — Which Land Rover models use the M57 Td6?
In Land Rover application, the M57 Td6 powered the Range Rover L322 from 2002 to 2006, badged as the TD6. The engine was also used across BMW's 3, 5, 6, 7 Series, X3, X5, and Z4 models.
5. Shared — Is the Land Rover M57 Td6 the same as BMW's version?
Yes — the M57D30 engine is mechanically identical across BMW and Land Rover fitments. Land Rover used a slightly detuned version (177 hp) compared to some BMW applications, but the core engine, block, and internals are the same.

Shared-cost note: Omitted — engine is exclusive to Land Rover in this ecosystem.
CTA line: → Compare K-Series 1.8/2.3 engine prices from UK specialists
SECTION 6 — FAQ
1. Cost — How much does a K-Series 1.8/2.3 engine replacement cost?
A reconditioned K-Series 1.8/2.3 typically costs £900–£1,800 supply only, with used units from £500–£900. Fitting adds £600–£1,000 depending on labour rates and vehicle access. Specialist K-Series rebuilds may cost more.
2. Reliability — Is the K-Series 1.8/2.3 a reliable engine?
The K-Series has a mixed reputation (2.5★). While the engine is lightweight and refined, its well-documented head gasket failure — exacerbated by the use of a low-torque stretch bolt design and inadequate cooling system — gives it a poor reliability record. However, correctly rebuilt examples with upgraded MLS gaskets and proper coolant are much more durable.
3. Common failure — What is the most common K-Series failure?
Head gasket failure is the most common and notorious issue — caused by the original elastomer gasket design and the use of stretch bolts that lose clamping force over time. Also common: coolant system leaks, thermostat housing failures, and liner movement in high-mileage engines.
4. Fitment — Which Land Rover models use the K-Series?
The K-Series powered the Freelander 1 (L314) in 1.8L (18K4F) and later 2.3L (23K4F) forms from 1997 to 2006.
5. Longevity — How long does the K-Series 1.8/2.3 last?
With the original elastomer head gasket and stretch bolts, many K-Series engines failed before 80,000 miles. However, correctly rebuilt engines using the later metal MLS (Multi-Layer Steel) head gasket and upgraded bolts often exceed 150,000–200,000 miles when properly maintained with the correct coolant.

SECTION 6 — FAQ
1. Cost — How much does an M47 (Td4) engine replacement cost?
A reconditioned M47 Td4 typically costs £1,500–£2,500 supply only, with used units from £500–£1,000. Fitting adds £700–£1,000 depending on labour rates and vehicle access.
2. Reliability — Is the BMW M47 (Td4) a reliable engine?
Yes — the M47 is considered one of BMW's most reliable diesel fours (4.0★), with many examples exceeding 200,000 miles when properly maintained. Its simplicity and robust construction make it a favourite among Freelander owners.
3. Common failure — What is the most common M47 failure?
Swirl flap failure is the most critical — the plastic flaps in the intake manifold can break off and be ingested by the engine, causing catastrophic damage. Other common issues include EGR valve clogging, turbocharger wear, and injector problems.
4. Fitment — Which Land Rover models use the M47?
In Land Rover application, the M47 Td4 powered the Freelander 1 (L314) from 2000 to 2006. The engine was also used across BMW's 3 Series (E46), 5 Series (E39), X3 (E83), and other models.
5. Shared — Is the Land Rover M47 the same as BMW's version?
Yes — the M47D20 engine is mechanically identical across BMW and Land Rover fitments. Land Rover Freelander applications used slightly different ECU calibrations and ancillaries, but the core engine, block, and internals are the same.

SECTION 6 — FAQ
1. Cost — How much does an M51 2.5 TDS engine replacement cost?
A reconditioned M51 2.5 TDS typically costs £3,000–£5,500 supply only, with used units from £1,500–£3,000. Fitting adds £1,000–£1,500 depending on labour rates and vehicle access.
2. Reliability — Is the BMW M51 2.5 TDS a reliable engine?
Yes — the M51 is considered one of BMW's most robust six-cylinder diesels (4.0★), with many examples exceeding 200,000–250,000 miles when properly maintained. Its mechanical injection system and iron-block construction make it exceptionally durable.
3. Common failure — What is the most common M51 failure?
Cooling system neglect is the most common cause of failure — the cooling system is vulnerable to corrosion and leaks, and overheating can cause head gasket failure. Injector pump wear (particularly on high-mileage examples) and glow plug issues are also common.
4. Fitment — Which Land Rover models use the M51?
In Land Rover application, the M51 2.5 TDS powered the Range Rover P38A from 1994 to 2002. The engine was also used across BMW's 3, 5, and 7 Series, and the E34 525tds.
5. Shared — Is the Land Rover M51 the same as BMW's version?
Yes — the M51D25 engine is mechanically identical across BMW and Land Rover fitments. Land Rover P38A applications used a slightly detuned version (136 hp) compared to some BMW applications, but the core engine, block, and internals are the same.

Shared‑cost note (Shared mode): Parts cost is identical across BMW and Land Rover applications; labour time varies slightly by engine bay access and subframe design.

SECTION 6 — FAQ
1. Cost — How much does an M62 4.4 V8 engine replacement cost?
A reconditioned M62 4.4 V8 typically costs £4,000–£6,000 supply only, with used units from £1,800–£3,200. Fitting adds £1,000–£1,800 depending on labour rates and vehicle access.
2. Reliability — Is the BMW M62 4.4 V8 a reliable engine?
The M62 has a mixed reputation (3.5★). While the engine is smooth, powerful, and fundamentally well‑built, the timing chain guides — made of brittle plastic — can fail catastrophically at around 100,000–150,000 miles. Regular coolant system maintenance is also essential.
3. Common failure — What is the most common M62 failure?
Timing chain guide failure is the most critical — the plastic guides become brittle with age and mileage, disintegrate, and allow the chain to slip or break, causing catastrophic valve/piston interference. Cooling system leaks, valley pan gasket failures, and oil leaks from the valve covers are also common.
4. Fitment — Which Land Rover models use the M62?
In Land Rover application, the M62 4.4 V8 powered the Range Rover P38A from 1994 to 2002. The engine was also used across BMW's 5 Series (E39), 7 Series (E38), and X5 (E53).
5. Shared — Is the Land Rover M62 the same as BMW's version?
Yes — the M62B44 engine is mechanically identical across BMW and Land Rover fitments. Land Rover P38A applications used a slightly detuned version (280 hp) compared to some BMW applications, but the core engine, block, and internals are the same.

SECTION 6 — FAQ
1. Cost — How much does an N62 4.4 V8 engine replacement cost?
A reconditioned N62 4.4 V8 typically costs £3,500–£5,500 supply only, with used units from £1,500–£3,000. Fitting adds £1,000–£1,800 depending on labour rates and vehicle access.
2. Reliability — Is the BMW N62 4.4 V8 a reliable engine?
The N62 has a mixed reputation (3.5★). While it offers excellent performance and refinement, it is known for valve stem seal wear (causing blue smoke on startup) and cooling system leaks. Regular maintenance is essential, and some repairs are costly.
3. Common failure — What is the most common N62 failure?
Valve stem seal wear is the most common issue — causing blue smoke on startup and oil consumption. Cooling system leaks (water pump, thermostat housing, and expansion tank) and alternator bracket oil leaks are also well‑documented. Timing chain guide issues are less common than on the earlier M62.
4. Fitment — Which Land Rover models use the N62?
In Land Rover application, the N62 4.4 V8 powered the Range Rover L322 from 2002 to 2005. The engine was also used across BMW's 5 Series (E60), 6 Series (E63/E64), 7 Series (E65/E66), and X5 (E53).
5. Shared — Is the Land Rover N62 the same as BMW's version?
Yes — the N62B44 engine is mechanically identical across BMW and Land Rover fitments. Land Rover L322 applications used a slightly detuned version compared to some BMW applications, but the core engine, block, and internals are the same.

SECTION 6 — FAQ
1. Cost — How much does an SI6 (B6324S) engine replacement cost?
A reconditioned SI6 3.2 typically costs £2,200–£3,500 supply only, with used units from £800–£1,600. Fitting adds £800–£1,500 depending on labour rates and vehicle access.
2. Reliability — Is the Volvo SI6 (B6324S) a reliable engine?
Yes — the SI6 is considered a reliable and refined petrol engine (4.0★). Its smooth inline‑six design offers excellent power delivery and durability. However, early examples (2006–2009) have reported timing chain tensioner issues, so service history is critical.
3. Common failure — What is the most common SI6 failure?
Timing chain tensioner failure is the most critical — particularly on early engines (2006–2009) where the tensioner design was prone to failure, causing chain stretch and catastrophic valve/piston interference. Oil consumption and oil leaks from the timing cover are also reported.
4. Fitment — Which Land Rover models use the SI6?
In Land Rover application, the SI6 (B6324S) powered the Freelander 2 (L359) from 2006 to 2014. The engine was also used across Volvo's XC60, XC90, S80, and V70 models.
5. Longevity — How long does the SI6 (B6324S) last?
With proper maintenance and early timing chain tensioner replacement where needed, SI6 engines routinely exceed 150,000–200,000 miles. Regular oil changes and chain inspections are key to achieving this lifespan, particularly on pre‑2010 examples.

SECTION 6 — FAQ
1. Cost — How much does a PT204 (2.0 Si4 GTDi) engine replacement cost?
A reconditioned PT204 typically costs £2,995–£3,650 supply only, varying by power output and specification. Used units can be found from £1,800–£2,800, but provenance is critical. Fitting adds £900–£1,500 depending on labour rates.
2. Reliability — Is the PT204 (2.0 Si4 GTDi) a reliable engine?
The PT204 has a mixed reputation (3.5★). It offers strong performance and decent economy, but early examples (2017–2019) have reported cooling system issues, timing chain stretch, and phase regulator problems. Later revisions are more dependable.
3. Common failure — What is the most common PT204 failure?
The most common issues include: cooling system leaks and charge air pipe tears (early examples), crankshaft pulley bolt issues causing oil pump problems, Ti‑VCT phase regulator wear, and timing chain stretch requiring replacement around 150,000 km (~93,000 miles). Turbo lag and high‑RPM noise are also reported.
4. Fitment — Which Land Rover models use the PT204?
The PT204 powers the Defender (L663), Discovery 5 (L462), Discovery Sport (L550), Evoque (L538/L551), Range Rover (L405), Range Rover Sport (L494), and Velar (L560) — spanning 200–300 hp outputs across P200, P250, and P300 variants.
5. Shared — Is the Land Rover PT204 the same as Jaguar's version?
Yes — the PT204 is shared with Jaguar fitments (AJ200P / 204PT) in the XE, XF, F‑Pace, and E‑Pace. The engine is mechanically identical, though ECU calibrations and ancillaries differ by model.

   * Enquiry figure verification: The 480 figure is the [EM-VERIFIED] request volume for Land Rover 204PT from the proprietary data file (row 19). The PT204 is the Ingenium petrol equivalent of the 204PT.
   * Naming reconciliation: The "Ford Si4 GTDi" naming is a legacy conflation — the PT204 is a JLR‑developed Ingenium engine, assembled in England since 2017. It shares some EcoBoost lineage but is JLR's own design. The page uses "PT204 (2.0 Si4 GTDi)" as the primary identifier to match the URL, while acknowledging the correct JLR Ingenium provenance.

SECTION 6 — FAQ
1. Cost — How much does a 368DT (3.6 TDV8) engine replacement cost?
A reconditioned 368DT TDV8 typically costs £5,500–£8,000 supply only, varying by specification and rebuild quality. Used units can be found from £3,000–£5,000, but provenance is critical. Fitting adds £1,000–£2,000 depending on labour rates.
2. Reliability — Is the 368DT (3.6 TDV8) a reliable engine?
The 368DT has a poor reputation (3.0★). While it offers strong V8 torque and refinement, the early engines (2006–2009) are known for timing chain tensioner failure and, in more severe cases, crankshaft fracture. It is not the reliable 4.4 TDV8 (448DT) that replaced it.
3. Common failure — What is the most common 368DT failure?
Timing chain tensioner failure is the most critical on early (2006–2009) engines — causing chain slack, timing drift, and catastrophic valve/piston interference. Turbo actuator failure is also common (typically sticky vanes). The most severe risk is crankshaft fracture, which can occur without warning and writes off the engine.
4. Fitment — Which Land Rover models use the 368DT?
The 368DT powered the Range Rover L322 TDV8 from 2006 to 2009 and the Range Rover Sport L320 TDV8 from 2006 to 2012.
5. Longevity — How long does the 368DT (3.6 TDV8) last?
With meticulous maintenance — regular oil changes with correct spec, early timing chain tensioner replacement on pre‑2009 examples, and attentive listening for cold‑start rattle — 368DT engines can reach 150,000+ miles. However, many fail well before this due to the known issues. Later (2009+) examples are more durable but still require careful maintenance.

SECTION 6 — FAQ
1. Cost — How much does an AJ‑V8 4.2/4.4 Supercharged engine replacement cost?
A reconditioned AJ‑V8 supercharged typically costs £3,500–£5,500 supply only, with used units from £2,500–£4,000. Fitting adds £1,000–£2,000 depending on labour rates and supercharger plumbing complexity.
2. Reliability — Is the AJ‑V8 4.2/4.4 Supercharged a reliable engine?
The AJ‑V8 has a mixed reputation (3.5★). It offers glorious V8 power and a legendary soundtrack, but pre‑2012 examples are known for cooling system issues (water pump, crossover pipes) and timing chain guide wear. Post‑2012 revisions addressed many of these concerns.
3. Common failure — What is the most common AJ‑V8 supercharged failure?
Cooling system leaks are the most common — including water pump failure, thermostat housing cracks, and coolant crossover pipe corrosion. Timing chain guide wear (pre‑2012) and supercharger coupler wear (causing rattles) are also well‑documented. Oil leaks from the valve covers are common on higher‑mileage examples.
4. Fitment — Which Land Rover models use the AJ‑V8 supercharged?
The 4.2 SC powered the Range Rover L322 (2005–2009) and Range Rover Sport L320 (2006–2009). The 4.4 SC powered the L322 (2010–2012) and early L405 (2012–2013).
5. Shared — Is the Land Rover AJ‑V8 the same as Jaguar's version?
Yes — the AJ‑V8 supercharged engine is shared with Jaguar fitments in the XKR, XFR, XJ, and XK. The engine is mechanically identical, though ECU calibrations and ancillaries differ by model.

SECTION 6 — FAQ
1. Cost — How much does a P510 (Ingenium 3.0 I6 Twin-Turbo) engine replacement cost?
A reconditioned P510 twin‑turbo typically costs £4,500–£7,500 supply only, varying by specification. Used units can be found from £2,800–£4,800, but provenance is critical. Fitting adds £1,000–£2,000 depending on labour rates.
2. Reliability — Is the P510 (Ingenium 3.0 I6 Twin-Turbo) a reliable engine?
The P510 is a modern, high‑performance engine (4.0★) with promising real‑world feedback. However, its high state of tune and twin‑turbo configuration place additional stress on the cooling system. Regular maintenance is absolutely essential. Long‑term reliability data is still emerging.
3. Common failure — What is the most common P510 failure?
Cooling system stress is the primary concern — the high‑output tune generates significant heat, requiring meticulous coolant system maintenance. Charge air cooler leaks and turbo actuator issues have been reported on early examples. The MHEV system (48V) has also had some software‑related glitches.
4. Fitment — Which Land Rover models use the P510?
The P510 powers the Range Rover (L460), Range Rover Sport (L461), and Defender (L663) — representing the highest‑output Ingenium petrol variant at 510 PS.
5. Shared — Is the Land Rover P510 the same as Jaguar's version?
Yes — the P510 is shared with Jaguar fitments (F‑Pace SVR‑spec variants). The engine is mechanically identical, though ECU calibrations and ancillaries differ by model.

   * Service schema price range: LowPrice = £2,800 (lowest Used supply‑only from Section 5); highPrice = £10,500 (highest Rebuilt supply‑only from Section 5). Both are [INDUSTRY ESTIMATE] as tagged in source content.
   * Organization used: Organization (not LocalBusiness) — confirmed per requirement.
   * Publish / Modified dates: 2026-07-14 (placeholder; to be updated at publication).
   * ItemList (Block 2) and FAQPage (Block 3): Contain exactly the same entries as Sections 4 and 6 of the published content — no additions or omissions.
   * Enquiry figure verification: The EM_Proprietary_Data file does not contain a dedicated P510 entry. The page uses [ESTIMATED] and [Data Pending] as tagged placeholders.
   * Correction applied (internal): The AI Handover Summary notes: "P510 (Ingenium 3.0 I6 Twin-Turbo) — [VERIFY] flagged on both sheets — possibly a higher state of tune of AJ20P6 rather than a fully separate family; confirm before deciding 1 page vs. fold-in." This page treats P510 as a distinct variant within the Ingenium 3.0 I6 petrol family. If confirmed as identical to AJ20P6, this page should be merged/redirected to the AJ20P6 page.
